</form>        </div>

Paterson\n- name: Eyal Ronen\n- name: Eylon Yogev\ntarget: \u003ca href=\"https://eprint.iacr.org/2022/065\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ehttps://eprint.iacr.org/2022/065\u003c/a\u003e\nFIPS-140-3-IG:\ntitle: Implementation Guidance for FIPS 140-3 and the Cryptographic Module Validation Program\ntarget: \u003ca href=\"https://csrc.nist.gov/csrc/media/Projects/cryptographic-module-validation-program/documents/fips%20140-3/FIPS%20140-3%20IG.pdf\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ehttps://csrc.nist.gov/csrc/media/Projects/cryptographic-module-validation-program/documents/fips%20140-3/FIPS%20140-3%20IG.pdf\u003c/a\u003e\nauthor:\n- org: National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST)\ndate: July 26, 2024\nETSI.TS.103.744:\ntitle: \"ETSI TS 103 744 V1.2.1 CYBER-QSC; Quantum-safe Hybrid Key Establishment\"\ntarget: \u003ca href=\"https://www.etsi.org/deliver/etsi_ts/103700_103799/103744/01.02.01_60/ts_103744v010201p.pdf\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ehttps://www.etsi.org/deliver/etsi_ts/103700_103799/103744/01.02.01_60/ts_103744v010201p.pdf\u003c/a\u003e\nauthor:\n- org: ETSI\ndate: 2025-03\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e--- abstract\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis document defines combinations of US NIST ML-KEM [FIPS.203] in hybrid with traditional algorithms RSA-OAEP, ECDH, X25519, and X448. These combinations are tailored to meet security best practices and regulatory guidelines. Composite ML-KEM is applicable in any application that uses X.509 or PKIX data structures that accept ML-KEM, but where the operator wants extra protection against breaks or catastrophic bugs in ML-KEM.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e--- middle\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eIntroduction {#sec-intro}\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-introduction-sec-intro\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Introduction {#sec-intro}\" href=\"#introduction-sec-intro\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe advent of quantum computing poses a significant threat to current cryptographic systems because traditional cryptographic key establishment algorithms such as RSA-OAEP, Diffie-Hellman and its elliptic curve variants will become vulnerable to quantum attacks.\nUnlike previous migrations between cryptographic algorithms, this migration gives us the foresight that traditional cryptographic algorithms will be broken in the future, but will remain strong in the interim, the only uncertainty is around the timing. But there are also some novel challenges.\nFor instance, the aggressive migration timelines may require deploying PQC algorithms before their implementations have been fully hardened or certified, and dual-algorithm data protection may be desirable over a longer time period to hedge against security vulnerabilities and other implementation flaws in the new implementations.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eCautious implementers may opt to combine cryptographic algorithms in such a way that an attacker would need to break all of them simultaneously to compromise the protected data. These mechanisms are referred to as \"Post-Quantum / Traditional (PQ/T) Hybrids\" {{RFC9794}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis specification defines a specific instantiation of the PQ/T Hybrid paradigm called \"composite\" where multiple cryptographic algorithms are combined to form a single key encapsulation mechanism (KEM). The composite KEM presents a single public key and ciphertext such that it can be treated as a single atomic algorithm at the protocol level. This provides a property referred to as \"protocol backwards compatibility\" since it can be applied to protocols that are not explicitly hybrid-aware. The idea of a composite was first presented in {{Bindel2017}}.\nComposite algorithms retain some security even if one of their component algorithms is broken, which is discussed in detail in {{sec-cons}}.\nThis specification creates PQ/T Hybrids with ML-KEM, defined in [FIPS.203] as the PQ component.\nInstantiations of the composite ML-KEM scheme are provided based on ML-KEM, RSA-OAEP and ECDH.\nThe full list of algorithms registered by this specification is in {{sec-alg-parms}}.\nBackwards compatibility in the sense of upgraded systems continuing to interoperate with legacy systems is not directly covered in this specification, but is the subject of {{sec-backwards-compat}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eCertain jurisdictions have recommended that ML-KEM be used exclusively within a PQ/T hybrid framework. The use of a composite scheme provides a straightforward implementation of hybrid solutions compatible with (and advocated by) some governments and cybersecurity agencies [BSI2021], [ANSSI2024].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn some situations it might be possible to add Post-Quantum, via a PQ/T Hybrid, to an already audited and compliant solution without invalidating the existing certification, whereas a full replacement of the traditional cryptography would almost certainly incur regulatory and compliance delays. In other words, PQ/T Hybrids can allow for deploying Post-Quantum Cryptography before the PQ modules and operational procedures are fully audited and certified. This, more than any other requirement, is what motivates the large number of algorithm combinations in this specification: The intention is to provide a stepping stone from which any cryptographic algorithm an organization has deployed today can evolve or transition.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhile this specification registers a large number of composite algorithms, it is expected that organizations will choose to deploy a single composite algorithm, or a small number of composite algorithms, that meets the needs of their environment, and very few implementers will need concern themselves with the entire list. This specification does not specify any mandatory-to-implement algorithms, but {{sec-impl-profile}} provides a short-list of recommended composite algorithms for common use-cases.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite ML-KEM is applicable in any PKIX-related application that would otherwise use ML-KEM.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eConventions and Terminology {#sec-terminology}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-conventions-and-terminology-sec-terminology\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Conventions and Terminology {#sec-terminology}\" href=\"#conventions-and-terminology-sec-terminology\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{::boilerplate bcp14+}\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis specification is consistent with all terminology from {{RFC9794}}.\nIn addition, the following terms are used in this specification:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eALGORITHM\u003c/strong\u003e:\nThe usage of the term \"algorithm\" within this\nspecification generally refers to any function which\nhas a registered Object Identifier (OID) for\nuse within an ASN.1 AlgorithmIdentifier.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eApplication Backwards Compatibility\u003c/strong\u003e: The usual definition of backwards compatibility, meaning whether an upgraded and non-upgraded application can successfully establish communication.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCOMBINER\u003c/strong\u003e:\nA combiner specifies how multiple shared secret keys are combined\ninto a single shared secret key.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCOMPOSITE CRYPTOGRAPHIC ELEMENT\u003c/strong\u003e: {{RFC9794}} defines composites as: A\ncryptographic element that\nincorporates multiple component cryptographic elements of the same\ntype in a multi-algorithm scheme.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCOMPONENT / PRIMITIVE\u003c/strong\u003e:\nThe words \"component\" or \"primitive\" are used interchangeably\nto refer to a cryptographic algorithm that is used internally\nwithin a composite algorithm. For example this could be an\nasymmetric algorithm such as \"ML-KEM-768\" or \"RSA-OAEP\".\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDER:\u003c/strong\u003e\nDistinguished Encoding Rules as defined in [X.690].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eKEM:\u003c/strong\u003e\nA key encapsulation mechanism as defined in {{sec-kems}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePKI:\u003c/strong\u003e\nPublic Key Infrastructure, as defined in {{RFC5280}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePost-Quantum Traditional (PQ/T) hybrid scheme\u003c/strong\u003e:\nA multi-algorithm scheme where at least one component algorithm is a post-quantum algorithm and at least one is a traditional algorithm.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eProtocol Backwards Compatibility\u003c/strong\u003e: A property whereby a new feature can be added to a protocol without requiring any changes to the protocol's specification and only minimal changes to its implementations (such as adding new identifiers). This is notable because many PQ/T Hybrids require modification of the protocol to make it \"hybrid aware\", whereas this specification presents as a standalone algorithm and thus can take advantage of existing cryptographic agility mechanisms.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSHARED SECRET KEY:\u003c/strong\u003e\nA value established between two communicating parties for use as\ncryptographic key material suitable for direct use by symmetric\ncryptographic algorithms. This specification is concerned with shared\nsecrets established via public key cryptographic operations.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eNotation\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-notation\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Notation\" href=\"#notation\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe algorithm descriptions use python-like syntax. The following symbols deserve special mention:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e||\u003c/code\u003e represents concatenation of two byte arrays.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e[:]\u003c/code\u003e represents byte array slicing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e(a, b)\u003c/code\u003e represents a pair of values \u003ccode\u003ea\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eb\u003c/code\u003e. Typically this indicates that a function returns multiple values; the exact conveyance mechanism -- tuple, struct, output parameters, etc -- is left to the implementer.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e(a, _)\u003c/code\u003e: represents a pair of values where one -- the second one in this case -- is ignored.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eFunc\u0026lt;TYPE\u0026gt;()\u003c/code\u003e: represents a function that is parametrized by \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;TYPE\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e meaning that the function's implementation will have minor differences depending on the underlying TYPE. Typically this means that a function will need to look up different constants or use different underlying cryptographic primitives depending on which composite algorithm it is implementing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite Design Philosophy\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-composite-design-philosophy\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Composite Design Philosophy\" href=\"#composite-design-philosophy\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite algorithms, as defined in this specification, follow the definition in [RFC9794] and should be regarded as a single algorithm that performs a single cryptographic operation typical of a key establishment mechanism.This generally means that the complexity of combining algorithms can and should be handled by the cryptographic library or cryptographic module. The design intent is that protocols such as PKCS#10 [RFC2986], CMP [RFC4210], X.509 [RFC5280], the CMS [RFC5652], and the Trust Anchor Format [RFC5914] can treat composite algorithms as they would any other algorithm without the protocol layer to have any \"hybrid-awareness\". This is a property referred to as \"protocol backwards-compatibility\".\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDiscussion of the specific choices of algorithm pairings can be found in {{sec-rationale}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eOverview of the Composite ML-KEM Scheme {#sec-kems}\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-overview-of-the-composite-ml-kem-scheme-sec-kems\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Overview of the Composite ML-KEM Scheme {#sec-kems}\" href=\"#overview-of-the-composite-ml-kem-scheme-sec-kems\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite ML-KEM is a PQ/T hybrid Key Encapsulation Mechanism (KEM) which combines ML-KEM as specified in [FIPS.203] and {{I-D.ietf-lamps-kyber-certificates}} with one of RSA-OAEP defined in [RFC8017], the Elliptic Curve Diffie-Hellman key agreement schemes ECDH defined in section 5.7.1.2 of [SP.800-56Ar3], and X25519 / X448 defined in [RFC8410]. A KEM combiner function is used to combine the two component shared secret keys into a single shared secret key.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite Key Encapsulation Mechanisms are defined as cryptographic primitives that consist of three algorithms. These definitions are borrowed from {{RFC9180}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eKeyGen() -\u0026gt; (pk, sk)\u003c/code\u003e: A probabilistic key generation algorithm,\nwhich generates a public key \u003ccode\u003epk\u003c/code\u003e and a secret key \u003ccode\u003esk\u003c/code\u003e. Some cryptographic modules may also expose a \u003ccode\u003eKeyGen(seed) -\u0026gt; (pk, sk)\u003c/code\u003e, which generates \u003ccode\u003epk\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003esk\u003c/code\u003e deterministically from a seed. This specification assumes a seed-based keygen for ML-KEM.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eEncap(pk) -\u0026gt; (ss, ct)\u003c/code\u003e: A probabilistic encapsulation algorithm,\nwhich takes as input a public key \u003ccode\u003epk\u003c/code\u003e and outputs a ciphertext \u003ccode\u003ect\u003c/code\u003e\nand shared secret key \u003ccode\u003ess\u003c/code\u003e. Note: this specification uses \u003ccode\u003eEncap()\u003c/code\u003e to conform to {{?RFC9180}},\nbut [FIPS.203] uses \u003ccode\u003eEncaps()\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDecap(sk, ct) -\u0026gt; ss\u003c/code\u003e: A decapsulation algorithm, which takes as\ninput a secret key \u003ccode\u003esk\u003c/code\u003e and ciphertext \u003ccode\u003ect\u003c/code\u003e and outputs a shared\nsecret \u003ccode\u003ess\u003c/code\u003e, or in some cases a distinguished error value.\nNote: this specification uses \u003ccode\u003eDecap()\u003c/code\u003e to conform to {{RFC9180}},\nbut [FIPS.203] uses \u003ccode\u003eDecaps()\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe KEM interface was chosen as the interface for a composite key establishment because it allows for arbitrary combinations of component algorithm types since both key transport and key agreement mechanisms can be promoted into KEMs as described in {{sec-RSAOAEPKEM}} and {{sec-DHKEM}} below.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following algorithms are defined for serializing and deserializing component values. These algorithms are inspired by similar algorithms in {{RFC9180}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eSerializePublicKey(mlkemPK, tradPK) -\u0026gt; bytes\u003c/code\u003e: Produce a byte string encoding of the component public keys.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDeserializePublicKey(bytes) -\u0026gt; (mlkemPK, tradPK)\u003c/code\u003e: Parse a byte string to recover the component public keys.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eSerializeCiphertext(mlkemCT, tradCT) -\u0026gt; bytes\u003c/code\u003e: Produce a byte string encoding of the component ciphertexts.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDeserializeCiphertext(bytes) -\u0026gt; (mlkemCT, tradCT)\u003c/code\u003e: Parse a byte string to recover the component ciphertexts.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eSerializePrivateKey(mlkemSeed, tradSK) -\u0026gt; bytes\u003c/code\u003e: Produce a byte string encoding of the component private keys.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDeserializePrivateKey(bytes) -\u0026gt; (mlkemSeed, tradSK)\u003c/code\u003e: Parse a byte string to recover the component private keys.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFull definitions of serialization and deserialization algorithms can be found in {{sec-serialization}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePromotion of RSA-OAEP into a KEM {#sec-RSAOAEPKEM}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-promotion-of-rsa-oaep-into-a-kem-sec-rsaoaepkem\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Promotion of RSA-OAEP into a KEM {#sec-RSAOAEPKEM}\" href=\"#promotion-of-rsa-oaep-into-a-kem-sec-rsaoaepkem\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe RSA Optimal Asymmetric Encryption Padding (OAEP), as defined in section 7.1 of [RFC8017] is a public key encryption algorithm used to transport key material from a sender to a receiver. A \"key transport\" type algorithm has the following API:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eEncrypt(pk, ss) -\u0026gt; ct\u003c/code\u003e: Take an existing shared secret key \u003ccode\u003ess\u003c/code\u003e and encrypt it for \u003ccode\u003epk\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDecrypt(sk, ct) -\u0026gt; ss\u003c/code\u003e: Decrypt the ciphertext \u003ccode\u003ect\u003c/code\u003e to recover \u003ccode\u003ess\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote the difference between the API of \u003ccode\u003eRSA.Encrypt(pk, ss) -\u0026gt; ct\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eKEM.Encap(pk) -\u0026gt; (ss, ct)\u003c/code\u003e presented above. For this reason, RSA-OAEP cannot be directly combined with ML-KEM. Fortunately, a key transport mechanism such as RSA-OAEP can be easily promoted into a KEM by having the sender generate a random 256 bit shared secret key and encrypt it.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"RSAOAEPKEM.Encap(pkR):\n  shared_secret = SecureRandom(ss_len)\n  enc = RSAES-OAEP-ENCRYPT(pkR, shared_secret)\n\n  return shared_secret, enc\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eRSAOAEPKEM.Encap(pkR):\n  shared_secret = SecureRandom(ss_len)\n  enc = RSAES-OAEP-ENCRYPT(pkR, shared_secret)\n\n  return shared_secret, enc\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote that the OAEP label \u003ccode\u003eL\u003c/code\u003e is left to its default value, which is the empty string as per [RFC8017]. The shared secret key output by the overall Composite ML-KEM already binds a composite KEM Combiner Label, so there is no need to also use the component Label.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe value of \u003ccode\u003ess_len\u003c/code\u003e as well as concrete values for all the RSA-OAEP parameters used within this specification can be found in {{sect-rsaoaep-params}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDecap(sk, ct) -\u0026gt; ss\u003c/code\u003e is accomplished by direct use of OAEP Decrypt.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"RSAOAEPKEM.Decap(skR, enc):\n  shared_secret = RSAES-OAEP-DECRYPT(skR, enc)\n\n  return shared_secret\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eRSAOAEPKEM.Decap(skR, enc):\n  shared_secret = RSAES-OAEP-DECRYPT(skR, enc)\n\n  return shared_secret\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe encodings for the public key (\u003ccode\u003epkR\u003c/code\u003e), private key (\u003ccode\u003eskR\u003c/code\u003e), and ciphertext (\u003ccode\u003eenc\u003c/code\u003e) are described in {{sec-serialization}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eA quick note on the choice of RSA-OAEP as the supported RSA encryption primitive. RSA-KEM [RFC5990] is cryptographically robust and is more straightforward to work with, but it has fairly limited adoption and therefore is of limited value as a PQ migration mechanism. Also, while RSA-PKCS#1v1.5 [RFC8017] is still widely used, it is hard to make secure and no longer FIPS-approved as of the end of 2023 [SP800-131Ar2], so it is of limited forwards value. This leaves RSA-OAEP [RFC8017] as the remaining choice. See {{sec-rationale}} for further discussion of algorithm choices.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote that, at least at the time of writing, the algorithm \u003ccode\u003eRSAOAEPKEM\u003c/code\u003e is not defined as a standalone algorithm within PKIX standards and it does not have an assigned algorithm OID, so it cannot be used directly with CMS KEMRecipientInfo [RFC9629]; it is merely a building block for the composite algorithm.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePromotion of ECDH into a KEM {#sec-DHKEM}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-promotion-of-ecdh-into-a-kem-sec-dhkem\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Promotion of ECDH into a KEM {#sec-DHKEM}\" href=\"#promotion-of-ecdh-into-a-kem-sec-dhkem\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe elliptic curve Diffie-Hellman algorithm identified by the OID \u003ccode\u003eid-ecDH\u003c/code\u003e as defined in [RFC5480] and [SEC1] is a key agreement algorithm requiring both parties to contribute an asymmetric keypair to the derivation of the shared secret key. A \"key agreement\" type algorithm has the following API:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDH(skX, pkY) -\u0026gt; ss\u003c/code\u003e: Each party combines their secret key \u003ccode\u003eskX\u003c/code\u003e with the other party's public key \u003ccode\u003epkY\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote the difference between the API of \u003ccode\u003eDH(skX, pkY) -\u0026gt; ss\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eKEM.Encap(pk) -\u0026gt; (ss, ct)\u003c/code\u003e presented above. For this reason, a Diffie-Hellman key exchange cannot be directly combined with ML-KEM. Fortunately, a Diffie-Hellman key agreement can be easily promoted into a KEM \u003ccode\u003eEncap(pk) -\u0026gt; (ss, ct)\u003c/code\u003e by having the sender generate an ephemeral keypair for themself and sending their public key as the ciphertext \u003ccode\u003ect\u003c/code\u003e. Composite ML-KEM uses a simplified version of the DHKEM definition from [RFC9180]:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"DHKEM.Encap(pkR):\n  (skE, pkE) = GenerateKeyPair()\n  ss = DH(skE, pkR)\n  ct = SerializePublicKey(pkE)\n\n  return ss, ct\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDHKEM.Encap(pkR):\n  (skE, pkE) = GenerateKeyPair()\n  ss = DH(skE, pkR)\n  ct = SerializePublicKey(pkE)\n\n  return ss, ct\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDecap(sk, ct) -\u0026gt; ss\u003c/code\u003e is accomplished in the analogous way.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"DHKEM.Decap(skR, ct):\n  pkE = DeserializePublicKey(ct)\n  ss = DH(skR, pkE)\n\n  return ss\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDHKEM.Decap(skR, ct):\n  pkE = DeserializePublicKey(ct)\n  ss = DH(skR, pkE)\n\n  return ss\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis construction applies for all variants of elliptic curve Diffie-Hellman used in this specification: ECDH, X25519, and X448.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor ECDH, \u003ccode\u003eDH()\u003c/code\u003e yields the value \u003ccode\u003eZ\u003c/code\u003e as described in section 5.7.1.2 of [SP.800-56Ar3].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor X25519 and X448, \u003ccode\u003eDH()\u003c/code\u003e yields the value \u003ccode\u003eK\u003c/code\u003e as described in section 6 of [RFC7748].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe encodings for the public key (\u003ccode\u003epkR\u003c/code\u003e), private key (\u003ccode\u003eskR\u003c/code\u003e), and ciphertext (\u003ccode\u003epkE\u003c/code\u003e) are described in {{sec-serialization}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe promotion of DH to a KEM is similar to the DHKEM functions in [RFC9180], but it is simplified in the following ways:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eNotation has been aligned to the notation used in this specification.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eSince a KEM Combiner Label is included explicitly in the Composite ML-KEM combiner, there is no need to perform the labeled steps of \u003ccode\u003eExtractAndExpand()\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eSince the ciphertext and receiver's public key are included explicitly in the Composite ML-KEM combiner, there is no need to construct the \u003ccode\u003ekem_context\u003c/code\u003e object.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote that here, \u003ccode\u003eSerializePublicKey()\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eDeserializePublicKey()\u003c/code\u003e refer to the underlying encoding of the DH primitive, and not to the composite serialization functions defined in {{sec-serialization}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote that, at least at the time of writing, the algorithm \u003ccode\u003eDHKEM\u003c/code\u003e is not defined as a standalone algorithm within PKIX standards and it does not have an assigned algorithm OID, so it cannot be used directly with CMS KEMRecipientInfo [RFC9629]; it is merely a building block for the composite algorithm.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite ML-KEM Functions {#sec-composite-mlkem}\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-composite-ml-kem-functions-sec-composite-mlkem\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Composite ML-KEM Functions {#sec-composite-mlkem}\" href=\"#composite-ml-kem-functions-sec-composite-mlkem\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis section describes the composite ML-KEM functions needed to instantiate the public API of a Key Encapsulation Mechanism as defined in {{sec-kems}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eKey Generation {#sec-keygen}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-key-generation-sec-keygen\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Key Generation {#sec-keygen}\" href=\"#key-generation-sec-keygen\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn order to maintain security properties of the composite, this specification\nstrictly forbids re-using component key material between composite and\nnon-composite keys, or between multiple composite keys. This means that an invocation of \u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM.KeyGen()\u003c/code\u003e MUST perform, or otherwise guarantee, fresh generation of the key material for both underlying algorithms and MUST NOT reuse existing key material. See {{sec-cons-key-reuse}} for a discussion.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTo generate a new keypair for composite schemes, the \u003ccode\u003eKeyGen() -\u0026gt; (pk, sk)\u003c/code\u003e function is used. The KeyGen() function calls the two key generation functions of the component algorithms independently. Multi-threaded, multi-process, or multi-module applications might choose to execute the key generation functions in parallel for better key generation performance or architectural modularity.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTo generate an ML-KEM key pair this specification uses the function \u003ccode\u003eML-KEM.KeyGen_internal(d, z)\u003c/code\u003e. According to [FIPS.203] d and z are two random 32 Byte values. This document combines both values in mlkemSeed by concatenating them so that \u003ccode\u003emlkemSeed = d || z\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following describes how to instantiate a \u003ccode\u003eKeyGen()\u003c/code\u003e function for a given composite algorithm represented by \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"Composite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.KeyGen() -\u0026gt; (pk, sk)\n\nExplicit Inputs:\n     None\n\nImplicit Inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM     The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n             parameter set, for example \u0026quot;ML-KEM-768\u0026quot;.\n\n  Trad       The underlying traditional algorithm and\n             parameter, for example \u0026quot;RSA-OAEP\u0026quot;\n             or \u0026quot;X25519\u0026quot;.\n\nOutput:\n  (pk, sk)  The composite keypair.\n\nKey Generation Process:\n\n  1. Generate component keys\n\n    mlkemSeed = Random(64)\n    (mlkemPK, mlkemSK) = ML-KEM.KeyGen_internal(mlkemSeed[:32], mlkemSeed[32:])\n    (tradPK, tradSK) = Trad.KeyGen()\n\n  2. Check for component key gen failure\n    if NOT (mlkemPK, mlkemSK) or NOT (tradPK, tradSK):\n      output \u0026quot;Key generation error\u0026quot;\n\n  3. Output the composite public and private keys\n\n    pk = SerializePublicKey(mlkemPK, tradPK)\n    sk = SerializePrivateKey(mlkemSeed, tradSK)\n    return (pk, sk)\n\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.KeyGen() -\u0026gt; (pk, sk)\n\nExplicit Inputs:\n     None\n\nImplicit Inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM     The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n             parameter set, for example \"ML-KEM-768\".\n\n  Trad       The underlying traditional algorithm and\n             parameter, for example \"RSA-OAEP\"\n             or \"X25519\".\n\nOutput:\n  (pk, sk)  The composite keypair.\n\nKey Generation Process:\n\n  1. Generate component keys\n\n    mlkemSeed = Random(64)\n    (mlkemPK, mlkemSK) = ML-KEM.KeyGen_internal(mlkemSeed[:32], mlkemSeed[32:])\n    (tradPK, tradSK) = Trad.KeyGen()\n\n  2. Check for component key gen failure\n    if NOT (mlkemPK, mlkemSK) or NOT (tradPK, tradSK):\n      output \"Key generation error\"\n\n  3. Output the composite public and private keys\n\n    pk = SerializePublicKey(mlkemPK, tradPK)\n    sk = SerializePrivateKey(mlkemSeed, tradSK)\n    return (pk, sk)\n\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn order to ensure fresh keys, the key generation functions MUST be executed for both component algorithms. Compliant parties MUST NOT use, import or export component keys that are used in other contexts, combinations, or by themselves as keys for standalone algorithm use. For more details on the security considerations around key reuse, see {{sec-cons-key-reuse}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eErrors produced by the component \u003ccode\u003eKeyGen()\u003c/code\u003e routines MUST be forwarded on to the calling application. Further discussion can be found below in {{sec-explicit-rejection}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eAllowed Modifications to the Key Generation Process\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-allowed-modifications-to-the-key-generation-process\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Allowed Modifications to the Key Generation Process\" href=\"#allowed-modifications-to-the-key-generation-process\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eKey generation is a process that is entirely internal to a cryptographic module, and as such it is often customized to fit the performance or operational requirements of the module. In cases where the private keys never leave the module or are otherwise not required to interoperate with other cryptographic modules, it is not required for interoperability for the private keys to match the format described in this specification. Therefore, in general, implementations of Composite ML-KEM MAY use an alternate key generation process so long as it generates compatible public keys, and so long as both component keys are freshly-generated and not re-used in a standalone key or within another composite key. Below are some examples of modifications that an implementer MAY make to the key generation process.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eImplementations MAY modify this process to additionally output the expanded \u003ccode\u003emlkemSK\u003c/code\u003e or to make use of \u003ccode\u003eML-KEM.KeyGen_internal(d, z)\u003c/code\u003e as needed to expand the ML-KEM seed \u003ccode\u003e(d || z)\u003c/code\u003e into an expanded key prior to performing a signing operation.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn cases where it is desirable to have a deterministic KeyGen of one or both component keys from a seed, this process MAY be modified to expose an interface of \u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.KeyGen(seed)\u003c/code\u003e such that one component algorithm is generated from the seed and the other from random, or the input seed is cryptohraphically expanded to produce seeds for both components. Security analysis of such a modified key generation process is outside the scope of this document.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhere interoperable private keys are not required, implementations MAY choose to use a different private key representation than the one given in {{sec-serialize-privkey}}. For example, the component keys MAY be stored in separate cryptographic modules, or MAY be stored in separate PKCS#8 objects, or MAY be stored in a format that preserves the ML-KEM expanded key instead of the ML-KEM seed. The required modifications to the key generation process, as well as the signature generation process below,  to support these private key representations are considered compliant with this specification so long as they generate compatible public keys, and so long as both component keys are freshly-generated. Note that when implementing Composite ML-KEM with a private key format that does not preserve the ML-KEM seed, especially when implementing on top of a cryptographic module that does not support seeds, it will be impossible to reconstruct a compliant seed-based private key as described in {{sec-serialize-privkey}}\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eEncapsulation\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-encapsulation\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Encapsulation\" href=\"#encapsulation\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eEncap(pk)\u003c/code\u003e of a Composite ML-KEM algorithm is designed to behave exactly the same as \u003ccode\u003eML-KEM.Encaps(ek)\u003c/code\u003e defined in Algorithm 20 in Section 7.2 of [FIPS.203]. Specifically, \u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM.Encap(pk)\u003c/code\u003e produces a 256-bit shared secret key that can be used directly with any symmetric-key cryptographic algorithm. In this way, Composite ML-KEM can be used as a direct drop-in replacement anywhere that ML-KEM is used.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following describes how to instantiate a \u003ccode\u003eEncap(pk)\u003c/code\u003e function for a given composite algorithm represented by \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"Composite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.Encap(pk) -\u0026gt; (ss, ct)\n\nExplicit Inputs:\n\n  pk      Composite public key consisting of encryption public keys\n          for each component.\n\nImplicit inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM  The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n          parameter set, for example \u0026quot;ML-KEM-768\u0026quot;.\n\n  Trad    The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n          parameter set, for example \u0026quot;RSA-OAEP\u0026quot;\n          or \u0026quot;X25519\u0026quot;.\n\n  Label   KEM Combiner Label value for binding the ciphertext to the\n          Composite OID. See section on KEM Combiner Labels below.\n\nOutput:\n\n  ss      The shared secret key, a 256-bit key suitable for use with\n          symmetric cryptographic algorithms.\n\n  ct      The ciphertext, a byte string.\n\nEncap Process:\n\n  1. Separate the public keys.\n\n      (mlkemPK, tradPK) = DeserializePublicKey(pk)\n\n  2.  Perform the respective component Encap operations according to\n      their algorithm specifications.\n\n      (mlkemCT, mlkemSS) = ML-KEM.Encaps(mlkemPK)\n      (tradCT, tradSS) = TradKEM.Encap(tradPK)\n\n  3. If either ML-KEM.Encaps() or TradKEM.Encap() return an error,\n     then this process must return an error.\n\n      if NOT (mlkemCT, mlkemSS) or NOT (tradCT, tradSS):\n        output \u0026quot;Encapsulation error\u0026quot;\n\n  4. Encode the ciphertext\n\n      ct = SerializeCiphertext(mlkemCT, tradCT)\n\n  5. Combine the KEM secrets and additional context to yield the\n     composite shared secret key.\n\n        ss = KemCombiner(mlkemSS, tradSS, tradCT, tradPK, Label)\n\n  6. Output composite shared secret key and ciphertext.\n\n     return (ss, ct)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.Encap(pk) -\u0026gt; (ss, ct)\n\nExplicit Inputs:\n\n  pk      Composite public key consisting of encryption public keys\n          for each component.\n\nImplicit inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM  The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n          parameter set, for example \"ML-KEM-768\".\n\n  Trad    The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n          parameter set, for example \"RSA-OAEP\"\n          or \"X25519\".\n\n  Label   KEM Combiner Label value for binding the ciphertext to the\n          Composite OID. See section on KEM Combiner Labels below.\n\nOutput:\n\n  ss      The shared secret key, a 256-bit key suitable for use with\n          symmetric cryptographic algorithms.\n\n  ct      The ciphertext, a byte string.\n\nEncap Process:\n\n  1. Separate the public keys.\n\n      (mlkemPK, tradPK) = DeserializePublicKey(pk)\n\n  2.  Perform the respective component Encap operations according to\n      their algorithm specifications.\n\n      (mlkemCT, mlkemSS) = ML-KEM.Encaps(mlkemPK)\n      (tradCT, tradSS) = TradKEM.Encap(tradPK)\n\n  3. If either ML-KEM.Encaps() or TradKEM.Encap() return an error,\n     then this process must return an error.\n\n      if NOT (mlkemCT, mlkemSS) or NOT (tradCT, tradSS):\n        output \"Encapsulation error\"\n\n  4. Encode the ciphertext\n\n      ct = SerializeCiphertext(mlkemCT, tradCT)\n\n  5. Combine the KEM secrets and additional context to yield the\n     composite shared secret key.\n\n        ss = KemCombiner(mlkemSS, tradSS, tradCT, tradPK, Label)\n\n  6. Output composite shared secret key and ciphertext.\n\n     return (ss, ct)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe specific values for \u003ccode\u003eLabel\u003c/code\u003e are defined per Composite ML-KEM algorithm in {{sec-alg-parms}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eErrors produced by the component \u003ccode\u003eEncaps()\u003c/code\u003e routines MUST be forwarded on to the calling application. Further discussion can be found below in {{sec-explicit-rejection}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eDecapsulation {#sect-composite-decaps}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-decapsulation-sect-composite-decaps\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Decapsulation {#sect-composite-decaps}\" href=\"#decapsulation-sect-composite-decaps\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eDecap(sk, ct) -\u0026gt; ss\u003c/code\u003e of a Composite ML-KEM algorithm is designed to behave exactly the same as \u003ccode\u003eML-KEM.Decaps(dk, c)\u003c/code\u003e defined in Algorithm 21 in Section 7.3 of [FIPS.203]. Specifically, \u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM.Decap(sk, ct)\u003c/code\u003e produces a 256-bit shared secret key that can be used directly with any symmetric-key cryptographic algorithm. In this way, Composite ML-KEM can be used as a direct drop-in replacement anywhere that ML-KEM is used.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following describes how to instantiate a \u003ccode\u003eDecap(sk, ct)\u003c/code\u003e function for a given composite algorithm represented by \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"Composite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.Decap(sk, ct) -\u0026gt; ss\n\nExplicit inputs\n\n  sk      Composite private key consisting of decryption private\n          keys for each component.\n\n  ct      The ciphertext, a byte string.\n\nImplicit inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM  The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n          parameter set, for example \u0026quot;ML-KEM-768\u0026quot;.\n\n  Trad    The underlying traditional algorithm and\n          parameter set, for example \u0026quot;RSA-OAEP\u0026quot;\n          or \u0026quot;X25519\u0026quot;.\n\n  Label   KEM Combiner Label value for binding the ciphertext to\n          the Composite ML-KEM OID.\n          See section on KEM Combiner Labels below.\n\nImplicit inputs looked up from SK:\n\n  tradPK  The traditional public key is required for the KEM\n          combiner.\n          For discussion of where to get this value, see the\n          Decapsulation Requires the Public Key section.\n\nOutput:\n\n  ss      The shared secret key, a 256-bit key suitable for use\n          with symmetric cryptographic algorithms.\n\nDecap Process:\n\n  1. Separate the private keys and ciphertexts\n\n      (mlkemSeed, tradSK) = DeserializePrivateKey(sk)\n      (_, mlkemSK) = ML-KEM.KeyGen(mlkemSeed[:32], mlkemSeed[32:])\n      (mlkemCT, tradCT) = DeserializeCiphertext(ct)\n\n  2.  Perform the respective component Decap operations according\n      to their algorithm specifications.\n\n      mlkemSS = ML-KEM.Decaps(mlkemSK, mlkemCT)\n      tradSS  = TradKEM.Decap(tradSK, tradCT)\n\n  3. If either ML-KEM.Decaps() or TradKEM.Decap() return an error,\n     then this process must return an error.\n\n      if NOT mlkemSS or NOT tradSS:\n        output \u0026quot;Decapsulation error\u0026quot;\n\n  4. Combine the KEM secrets and additional context to yield the\n     composite shared secret key.\n\n      ss = KemCombiner(mlkemSS, tradSS, tradCT, tradPK, Label)\n\n  5. Output composite shared secret key.\n\n     return ss\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.Decap(sk, ct) -\u0026gt; ss\n\nExplicit inputs\n\n  sk      Composite private key consisting of decryption private\n          keys for each component.\n\n  ct      The ciphertext, a byte string.\n\nImplicit inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM  The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n          parameter set, for example \"ML-KEM-768\".\n\n  Trad    The underlying traditional algorithm and\n          parameter set, for example \"RSA-OAEP\"\n          or \"X25519\".\n\n  Label   KEM Combiner Label value for binding the ciphertext to\n          the Composite ML-KEM OID.\n          See section on KEM Combiner Labels below.\n\nImplicit inputs looked up from SK:\n\n  tradPK  The traditional public key is required for the KEM\n          combiner.\n          For discussion of where to get this value, see the\n          Decapsulation Requires the Public Key section.\n\nOutput:\n\n  ss      The shared secret key, a 256-bit key suitable for use\n          with symmetric cryptographic algorithms.\n\nDecap Process:\n\n  1. Separate the private keys and ciphertexts\n\n      (mlkemSeed, tradSK) = DeserializePrivateKey(sk)\n      (_, mlkemSK) = ML-KEM.KeyGen(mlkemSeed[:32], mlkemSeed[32:])\n      (mlkemCT, tradCT) = DeserializeCiphertext(ct)\n\n  2.  Perform the respective component Decap operations according\n      to their algorithm specifications.\n\n      mlkemSS = ML-KEM.Decaps(mlkemSK, mlkemCT)\n      tradSS  = TradKEM.Decap(tradSK, tradCT)\n\n  3. If either ML-KEM.Decaps() or TradKEM.Decap() return an error,\n     then this process must return an error.\n\n      if NOT mlkemSS or NOT tradSS:\n        output \"Decapsulation error\"\n\n  4. Combine the KEM secrets and additional context to yield the\n     composite shared secret key.\n\n      ss = KemCombiner(mlkemSS, tradSS, tradCT, tradPK, Label)\n\n  5. Output composite shared secret key.\n\n     return ss\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSteps 2, 3, and 4 SHOULD be performed in a timing-invariant way to prevent side-channel attackers from learning which component algorithm failed and from learning any of the inputs or output of the KEM combiner.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eStep 4 requires the \u003ccode\u003eDecaps()\u003c/code\u003e process to have access to \u003ccode\u003etradPK\u003c/code\u003e, which is not carried in the private key format and therefore the implementation is required to acquire it from some out-of-band means. The Implementation Considerations {{impl-cons-decaps-pubkey}} provides further discussion on this.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIt is possible to use component private keys stored in separate software or hardware keystores. Variations in the process to accommodate particular private key storage mechanisms are considered to be conformant to this specification so long as it produces the same output and error handling as the process sketched above.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn order to properly achieve its security properties, the KEM combiner requires that all inputs are fixed-length or length-encoded. Since each Composite ML-KEM algorithm fully specifies its component algorithms, including key sizes, all inputs should be fixed-length in non-error scenarios except for minor variations introduced by encoding. In the cases where there are minor variations introduced by encoding, those encodings already have a fixed-length prefix followed by length-encoded data, so the requirements for the KEM combiner security properties hold (namely that the input is injective). However some implementations may choose to perform additional checking to handle certain error conditions. In particular, the KEM combiner step should not be performed if either of the component decapsulations returned an error condition indicating malformed inputs. RSA-based composites MUST ensure that the modulus size (i.e. the size of \u003ccode\u003etradCT\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003etradPK\u003c/code\u003e) matches that specified for the given Composite ML-KEM algorithm in {{sec-alg-parms}}; depending on the cryptographic library used, this check may be done by the library or may require an explicit check as part of the \u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM.Decap()\u003c/code\u003e routine. Implementers should keep in mind that some instances of \u003ccode\u003etradCT\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003etradPK\u003c/code\u003e will be DER-encoded which could introduce minor length variations such as dropping leading zeroes; since the underlying KEMs are assumed to be IND-CCA secure, decapsulation against tampered ciphertexts or public keys is assumed to fail, these length differences are considered benign to the KEM combiner.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eErrors produced by the component \u003ccode\u003eDecaps()\u003c/code\u003e routines MUST be forwarded on to the calling application. Further discussion can be found below in {{sec-explicit-rejection}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eKEM Combiner Function {#sec-kem-combiner}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-kem-combiner-function-sec-kem-combiner\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: KEM Combiner Function {#sec-kem-combiner}\" href=\"#kem-combiner-function-sec-kem-combiner\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis specification provides a combiner construction with SHA3-256 for all combinations of algorithms.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"KemCombiner(mlkemSS, tradSS, tradCT, tradPK, Label) -\u0026gt; ss\n\nExplicit inputs:\n\n  The list of input values to be combined.\n\nOutput:\n\n  ss      The shared secret key, a 256-bit key suitable for use with\n          symmetric cryptographic algorithms.\n\n\nProcess:\n\n  ss = SHA3-256(mlkemSS || tradSS || tradCT || tradPK || Label)\n\n  return ss\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eKemCombiner(mlkemSS, tradSS, tradCT, tradPK, Label) -\u0026gt; ss\n\nExplicit inputs:\n\n  The list of input values to be combined.\n\nOutput:\n\n  ss      The shared secret key, a 256-bit key suitable for use with\n          symmetric cryptographic algorithms.\n\n\nProcess:\n\n  ss = SHA3-256(mlkemSS || tradSS || tradCT || tradPK || Label)\n\n  return ss\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eError Handling and Explicit Rejection {#sec-explicit-rejection}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-error-handling-and-explicit-rejection-sec-explicit-rejection\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Error Handling and Explicit Rejection {#sec-explicit-rejection}\" href=\"#error-handling-and-explicit-rejection-sec-explicit-rejection\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eML-KEM, particularly its \u003ccode\u003eDecaps()\u003c/code\u003e defined in Algorithms 18 and 21 of [FIPS.203], is designed to be implicitly rejecting, meaning that a failure within the underlying PKE scheme due to a mangled ciphertext will not cause \u003ccode\u003eML-KEM.Decaps()\u003c/code\u003e to return an error, but instead any errors encountered during decapsulation are handled by producing a pseudo-random shared secret. \u003ccode\u003eML-KEM.Decaps()\u003c/code\u003e can, however return errors for example if the provided ciphertext or decapsulation private key is the wrong size.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn Composite ML-KEM, not all component algorithms will be implicitly rejecting, for example RSA-OAEP's \u003ccode\u003eDecrypt()\u003c/code\u003e can return an error if the padding is incorrect. In general, in the case that one of the component primitives generates an error during Composite ML-KEM KeyGen, Encaps, or Decaps, Composite ML-KEM MUST clear all buffers containing key material and forward the error to its caller; i.e. Composite ML-KEM MUST be explicitly rejecting whenever one of its components is. The same applies to Composite ML-KEM \u003ccode\u003eKeyGen()\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eEncaps()\u003c/code\u003e: Composite KEM MUST forward any errors produced by component algorithms.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eSerialization {#sec-serialization}\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-serialization-sec-serialization\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Serialization {#sec-serialization}\" href=\"#serialization-sec-serialization\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis section presents routines for serializing and deserializing composite public keys, private keys, and ciphertext values to bytes.\nThe functions defined in this section are considered internal implementation details and are referenced from within the public API definitions in {{sec-composite-mlkem}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDeserialization is possible because ML-KEM has fixed-length public keys, private keys (seeds), and ciphertext values as shown in the following table.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eAlgorithm\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003ePublic Key\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003ePrivate Key\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eCiphertext\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eML-KEM-768\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e1184\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e64\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e1088\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eML-KEM-1024\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e1568\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e64\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e1568\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e{: #tab-mlkem-sizes title=\"ML-KEM Sizes in bytes\"}\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor all serialization routines below, when these values are required to be carried in an ASN.1 structure, they are wrapped as described in {{sec-encoding-to-der}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhile ML-KEM has a single fixed-size representation for each of public key, private key, and ciphertext, the traditional component might allow multiple valid encodings; for example an elliptic curve public key, and therefore also ciphertext, might be validly encoded as either compressed or uncompressed [SEC1], or an RSA private key could be encoded in Chinese Remainder Theorem form [RFC8017]. In order to obtain interoperability, composite algorithms MUST use the following encodings of the underlying components:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eML-KEM\u003c/strong\u003e: MUST be encoded as specified in sections 7.1 and 7.2 of [FIPS.203], using a 64-byte seed \u003ccode\u003e(d || z)\u003c/code\u003e as the private key.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRSA\u003c/strong\u003e: the public key MUST be encoded as RSAPublicKey with the \u003ccode\u003e(n,e)\u003c/code\u003e public key representation as specified in A.1.1 of [RFC8017] and the private key representation as RSAPrivateKey specified in A.1.2 of [RFC8017] with version 0 and 'otherPrimeInfos' absent. An RSA-OAEP ciphertext MUST be encoded as specified in section 7.1.1 of {{RFC8017}}\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eECDH\u003c/strong\u003e: public key MUST be encoded as an uncompressed X9.62 [X9.62–2005], including the leading byte \u003ccode\u003e0x04\u003c/code\u003e indicating uncompressed. This is consistent with the encoding of \u003ccode\u003eECPoint\u003c/code\u003e as specified in section 2.2 of [RFC5480] when no ASN.1 OCTET STRING wrapping is present. The private key MUST be encoded as ECPrivateKey specified in [RFC5915] with 'NamedCurve' parameter set to the OID of the curve, but without the 'publicKey' field. The ciphertext MUST be encoded in the same manner as the public key.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eX25519 and X448\u003c/strong\u003e: the public key MUST be encoded as per section 5 of [RFC7748] and the private key is a 32 or 56 byte raw value for X25519 and X448 respectively. The ciphertext MUST be encoded in the same manner as the public key.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAll ASN.1 objects SHALL be encoded using DER on serialization.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eEven with fixed encodings for the traditional component, there may be slight differences in size of the encoded value due to, for example, encoding rules that drop leading zeroes. See {{sec-sizetable}} for further discussion of encoded size of each composite algorithm.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe deserialization routines described below do not check for well-formedness of the cryptographic material they are recovering. It is assumed that underlying cryptographic primitives will catch malformed values and raise an appropriate error.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eSerializePublicKey and DeserializePublicKey {#sec-serialize-pubkey}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-serializepublickey-and-deserializepublickey-sec-serialize-pubkey\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: SerializePublicKey and DeserializePublicKey {#sec-serialize-pubkey}\" href=\"#serializepublickey-and-deserializepublickey-sec-serialize-pubkey\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe serialization routine for keys simply concatenates the public keys of the component algorithms, as defined below:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"Composite-ML-KEM.SerializePublicKey(mlkemPK, tradPK) -\u0026gt; Combine and output the encoded public key\n\n     output mlkemPK || tradPK\n\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDeserialization reverses this process. Each component key is deserialized according to their respective specification as shown in {{appdx_components}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following describes how to instantiate a \u003ccode\u003eDeserializePublicKey(bytes)\u003c/code\u003e function for a given composite algorithm represented by \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"Composite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.DeserializePublicKey(bytes) -\u0026gt; (mlkemPK, tradPK)\n\nExplicit inputs:\n\n  bytes   An encoded composite public key.\n\nImplicit inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM   The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n           parameter, for example, could be \u0026quot;ML-KEM-768\u0026quot;.\n\nOutput:\n\n  mlkemPK  The ML-KEM public key, which is bytes.\n\n  tradPK   The traditional public key in the appropriate\n           encoding for the underlying component algorithm.\n\n\nDeserialization Process:\n\n  1. Parse each constituent encoded public key.\n       The length of the mlkemPK is known based on the size of\n       the ML-KEM component key length specified by the Object ID.\n\n     switch ML-KEM do\n        case ML-KEM-768:\n          mlkemPK = bytes[:1184]\n          tradPK  = bytes[1184:]\n        case ML-KEM-1024:\n          mlkemPK = bytes[:1568]\n          tradPK  = bytes[1568:]\n\n     Note that while ML-KEM has fixed-length keys, RSA\n     may not, depending on encoding, so rigorous length-checking\n     of the overall composite key is not always possible.\n\n  2. Output the component public keys\n\n     output (mlkemPK, tradPK)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.DeserializePublicKey(bytes) -\u0026gt; (mlkemPK, tradPK)\n\nExplicit inputs:\n\n  bytes   An encoded composite public key.\n\nImplicit inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM   The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n           parameter, for example, could be \"ML-KEM-768\".\n\nOutput:\n\n  mlkemPK  The ML-KEM public key, which is bytes.\n\n  tradPK   The traditional public key in the appropriate\n           encoding for the underlying component algorithm.\n\n\nDeserialization Process:\n\n  1. Parse each constituent encoded public key.\n       The length of the mlkemPK is known based on the size of\n       the ML-KEM component key length specified by the Object ID.\n\n     switch ML-KEM do\n        case ML-KEM-768:\n          mlkemPK = bytes[:1184]\n          tradPK  = bytes[1184:]\n        case ML-KEM-1024:\n          mlkemPK = bytes[:1568]\n          tradPK  = bytes[1568:]\n\n     Note that while ML-KEM has fixed-length keys, RSA\n     may not, depending on encoding, so rigorous length-checking\n     of the overall composite key is not always possible.\n\n  2. Each component key is deserialized according to their respective specification as shown in {{appdx_components}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following describes how to instantiate a \u003ccode\u003eDeserializePrivateKey(bytes)\u003c/code\u003e function. Since ML-KEM private keys are 64 bytes for all parameter sets, this function does not need to be parametrized.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"Composite-ML-KEM.DeserializePrivateKey(bytes)\n                                    -\u0026gt; (mlkemSeed, tradSK)\n\nExplicit inputs:\n\n  bytes   An encoded composite private key.\n\nImplicit inputs:\n\n  That an ML-KEM private key is 64 bytes for all parameter sets.\n\nOutput:\n\n  mlkemSeed  The ML-KEM private key, which consists of 32 Byte seed value d\n             concatenated with 32 Byte seed value z.\n\n  tradSK    The traditional private key in the appropriate\n             encoding for the underlying component algorithm.\n\n\nDeserialization Process:\n\n  1.
