Combine and output the encoded composite ciphertext\n\n     output mlkemCT || tradCT\n\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM.SerializeCiphertext(mlkemCT, tradCT) -\u0026gt; bytes\n\nExplicit inputs:\n\n  mlkemCT  The ML-KEM ciphertext, which is bytes.\n\n  tradCT   The traditional ciphertext in the appropriate\n           encoding for the underlying component algorithm.\n\nImplicit inputs:\n\n  None\n\nOutput:\n\n  bytes   The encoded composite ciphertext value.\n\n\nSerialization Process:\n\n  1. Combine and output the encoded composite ciphertext\n\n     output mlkemCT || tradCT\n\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDeserialization reverses this process.  Each component ciphertext is deserialized according to their respective specification as shown in {{appdx_components}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following describes how to instantiate a \u003ccode\u003eDeserializeCiphertext(bytes)\u003c/code\u003e function for a given composite algorithm represented by \u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"Composite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.DeserializeCiphertext(bytes)\n                                          -\u0026gt; (mlkemCT, tradCT)\n\nExplicit inputs:\n\n  bytes   An encoded composite ciphertext value.\n\nImplicit inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM   The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n           parameter, for example, could be \u0026quot;ML-KEM-768\u0026quot;.\n\nOutput:\n\n  mlkemCT  The ML-KEM ciphertext, which is bytes.\n\n  tradCT   The traditional ciphertext in the appropriate\n           encoding for the underlying component algorithm.\n\n\nDeserialization Process:\n\n  1. Parse each constituent encoded ciphertext.\n     The length of the mlkemCT is known based on the size of the\n     ML-KEM component ciphertext length specified by the Object ID.\n\n     switch ML-KEM do\n        case ML-KEM-768:\n          mlkemCT = bytes[:1088]\n          tradCT  = bytes[1088:]\n        case ML-KEM-1024:\n          mlkemCT= bytes[:1568]\n          tradCT  = bytes[1568:]\n\n  2. Output the component ciphertext values\n\n     output (mlkemCT, tradCT)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM\u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;.DeserializeCiphertext(bytes)\n                                          -\u0026gt; (mlkemCT, tradCT)\n\nExplicit inputs:\n\n  bytes   An encoded composite ciphertext value.\n\nImplicit inputs mapped from \u0026lt;OID\u0026gt;:\n\n  ML-KEM   The underlying ML-KEM algorithm and\n           parameter, for example, could be \"ML-KEM-768\".\n\nOutput:\n\n  mlkemCT  The ML-KEM ciphertext, which is bytes.\n\n  tradCT   The traditional ciphertext in the appropriate\n           encoding for the underlying component algorithm.\n\n\nDeserialization Process:\n\n  1. Parse each constituent encoded ciphertext.\n     The length of the mlkemCT is known based on the size of the\n     ML-KEM component ciphertext length specified by the Object ID.\n\n     switch ML-KEM do\n        case ML-KEM-768:\n          mlkemCT = bytes[:1088]\n          tradCT  = bytes[1088:]\n        case ML-KEM-1024:\n          mlkemCT= bytes[:1568]\n          tradCT  = bytes[1568:]\n\n  2. Output the component ciphertext values\n\n     output (mlkemCT, tradCT)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eUse within X.509 and PKIX\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-use-within-x509-and-pkix\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Use within X.509 and PKIX\" href=\"#use-within-x509-and-pkix\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following sections provide processing logic and the necessary ASN.1 modules necessary to use composite ML-KEM within X.509 and PKIX protocols. Use within the Cryptographic Message Syntax (CMS) will be covered in a separate specification.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhile composite ML-KEM keys and ciphertext values MAY be used raw, the following sections provide conventions for using them within X.509 and other PKIX protocols such that Composite ML-KEM can be used as a drop-in replacement for KEM algorithms in PKCS#10 [RFC2986], CMP [RFC4210], X.509 [RFC5280], and related protocols.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eEncoding to DER {#sec-encoding-to-der}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-encoding-to-der-sec-encoding-to-der\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Encoding to DER {#sec-encoding-to-der}\" href=\"#encoding-to-der-sec-encoding-to-der\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe serialization routines presented in {{sec-serialization}} produce raw binary values. When these values are required to be carried within a DER-encoded message format such as an X.509's \u003ccode\u003esubjectPublicKey\u003c/code\u003e or a \u003ccode\u003eOneAsymmetricKey.privateKey OCTET STRING\u003c/code\u003e [RFC5958], then the BIT STRING or OCTET STRING contains this raw byte string output of the appropriate serialization routine from {{sec-serialization}} without further encoding.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen a Composite ML-KEM\npublic key appears outside of a \u003ccode\u003eSubjectPublicKeyInfo\u003c/code\u003e type in an\nenvironment that uses ASN.1 encoding, it could be encoded as an OCTET\nSTRING by using the Composite-ML-KEM-PublicKey type defined below.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"Composite-ML-KEM-PublicKey ::= OCTET STRING\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eComposite-ML-KEM-PublicKey ::= OCTET STRING\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSize constraints MAY be enforced, as appropriate as per {{sec-sizetable}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eKey Usage viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 \u003ccode\u003eSubjectPublicKeyInfo.AlgorithmIdentifier\u003c/code\u003e field of an X.509 certificate [RFC5280], the key usage certificate extension MUST only contain:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"keyEncipherment\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ekeyEncipherment\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite ML-KEM keys MUST NOT be used in a \"dual usage\" mode because even if the\ntraditional component key supports both signing and encryption,\nthe post-quantum algorithms do not and therefore the overall composite algorithm does not. Implementations MUST NOT use one component of the composite for the purposes of digital signature and the other component for the purposes of encryption or key establishment.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eASN.1 Definitions {#sec-asn1-defs}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-asn1-definitions-sec-asn1-defs\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: ASN.1 Definitions {#sec-asn1-defs}\" href=\"#asn1-definitions-sec-asn1-defs\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite ML-KEM uses a substantially non-ASN.1 based encoding, as specified in {{sec-serialization}}. However, as composite algorithms will be used within ASN.1-based X.509 and PKIX protocols, some conventions for ASN.1 wrapping are necessary.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following ASN.1 Information Object Classes are defined to allow for compact definitions of each composite algorithm, leading to a smaller overall ASN.1 module.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-asn notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"pk-CompositeKEM {OBJECT IDENTIFIER:id}\n  PUBLIC-KEY ::= {\n    IDENTIFIER id\n    -- KEY no ASN.1 wrapping --\n    PARAMS ARE absent\n    CERT-KEY-USAGE { keyEncipherment }\n    -- PRIVATE-KEY no ASN.1 wrapping --\n  }\n\nkema-CompositeKEM {\n  OBJECT IDENTIFIER:id,\n    PUBLIC-KEY:publicKeyType }\n    KEM-ALGORITHM ::= {\n         IDENTIFIER id\n         -- VALUE no ASN.1 wrapping --\n         PARAMS ARE absent\n         PUBLIC-KEYS { publicKeyType }\n         SMIME-CAPS { IDENTIFIED BY id }\n        }\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003epk-CompositeKEM {\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eOBJECT IDENTIFIER\u003c/span\u003e:id}\n  PUBLIC-KEY \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e::=\u003c/span\u003e {\n    IDENTIFIER id\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e-- KEY no ASN.1 wrapping --\u003c/span\u003e\n    PARAMS ARE absent\n    CERT-KEY-USAGE { keyEncipherment }\n    \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e-- PRIVATE-KEY no ASN.1 wrapping --\u003c/span\u003e\n  }\n\nkema-CompositeKEM {\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eOBJECT IDENTIFIER\u003c/span\u003e:id,\n    PUBLIC-KEY:publicKeyType }\n    KEM-ALGORITHM \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e::=\u003c/span\u003e {\n         IDENTIFIER id\n         \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e-- VALUE no ASN.1 wrapping --\u003c/span\u003e\n         PARAMS ARE absent\n         PUBLIC-KEYS { publicKeyType }\n         SMIME-CAPS { IDENTIFIED BY id }\n        }\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: #asn1-info-classes title=\"ASN.1 Object Information Classes for Composite ML-KEM\"}\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAs an example, the public key and KEM algorithm types associated with \u003ccode\u003eid-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256\u003c/code\u003e are defined as:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"pk-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256 PUBLIC-KEY ::=\n  pk-CompositeKEM {\n    id-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256 }\n\nkema-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256 KEM-ALGORITHM ::=\n    kema-CompositeKEM{\n      id-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256,\n      pk-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256 }\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epk-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256 PUBLIC-KEY ::=\n  pk-CompositeKEM {\n    id-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256 }\n\nkema-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256 KEM-ALGORITHM ::=\n    kema-CompositeKEM{\n      id-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256,\n      pk-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256 }\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe full set of key types defined by this specification can be found in the ASN.1 Module in {{sec-asn1-module}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUse cases that require an interoperable encoding for composite private keys will often need to place a composite private key inside a \u003ccode\u003eOneAsymmetricKey\u003c/code\u003e structure defined in [RFC5958], such as when private keys are carried in PKCS #12 [RFC7292], CMP [RFC4210] or CRMF [RFC4211]. The definition of \u003ccode\u003eOneAsymmetricKey\u003c/code\u003e is copied here for convenience:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-asn notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\" OneAsymmetricKey ::= SEQUENCE {\n       version                   Version,\n       privateKeyAlgorithm       PrivateKeyAlgorithmIdentifier,\n       privateKey                PrivateKey,\n       attributes            [0] Attributes OPTIONAL,\n       ...,\n       [[2: publicKey        [1] PublicKey OPTIONAL ]],\n       ...\n     }\n\n  ...\n  PrivateKey ::= OCTET STRING\n                        -- Content varies based on type of key.  The\n                        -- algorithm identifier dictates the format of\n                        -- the key.\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e OneAsymmetricKey \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e::=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eSEQUENCE\u003c/span\u003e {\n       version                   Version,\n       privateKeyAlgorithm       PrivateKeyAlgorithmIdentifier,\n       privateKey                PrivateKey,\n       attributes            [0] Attributes \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eOPTIONAL\u003c/span\u003e,\n       \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e..\u003c/span\u003e.,\n       [[2: publicKey        [1] PublicKey \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eOPTIONAL\u003c/span\u003e ]],\n       \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e..\u003c/span\u003e.\n     }\n\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e..\u003c/span\u003e.\n  PrivateKey \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e::=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eOCTET STRING\u003c/span\u003e\n                        \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e-- Content varies based on type of key.  The\u003c/span\u003e\n                        \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e-- algorithm identifier dictates the format of\u003c/span\u003e\n                        \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e-- the key.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: artwork-name=\"RFC5958-OneAsymmetricKey-asn.1-structure\" title=\"OneAsymmetricKey as defined in [RFC5958]\"}\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen a composite private key is conveyed inside a \u003ccode\u003eOneAsymmetricKey\u003c/code\u003e structure (version 1 of which is also known as PrivateKeyInfo) [RFC5958], the \u003ccode\u003eprivateKeyAlgorithm\u003c/code\u003e field SHALL be set to the corresponding composite algorithm identifier defined according to {{sec-alg-parms}} and its parameters field MUST be absent.  The \u003ccode\u003eprivateKey\u003c/code\u003e field SHALL contain the OCTET STRING representation of the serialized composite private key as per {{sec-serialize-privkey}}. The \u003ccode\u003epublicKey\u003c/code\u003e field remains OPTIONAL. If the \u003ccode\u003epublicKey\u003c/code\u003e field is present, it MUST be a composite public key as per {{sec-serialize-pubkey}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSome applications might need to reconstruct the \u003ccode\u003eSubjectPublicKeyInfo\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003eOneAsymmetricKey\u003c/code\u003e objects corresponding to each component key individually, for example if this is required for invoking the underlying primitive. {{sec-alg-parms}} provides the necessary mapping between composite and their component algorithms for doing this reconstruction.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eComponent keys of a composite private key MUST NOT be used in any other type of key or as a standalone key. For more details on the security considerations around key reuse, see {{sec-cons-key-reuse}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eAlgorithm Identifiers and Parameters {#sec-alg-parms}\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-algorithm-identifiers-and-parameters-sec-alg-parms\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Algorithm Identifiers and Parameters {#sec-alg-parms}\" href=\"#algorithm-identifiers-and-parameters-sec-alg-parms\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis section lists the algorithm identifiers and parameters for all Composite ML-KEM algorithms.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFull specifications for the referenced algorithms can be found in {{appdx_components}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAs the number of algorithms can be daunting to implementers, see {{sec-impl-profile}} for a discussion of choosing a subset to support.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eEach Composite ML-KEM algorithm has a unique Label which is used in constructing the KEM combiner in ({{sec-kem-combiner}}). This helps protect against a different algorithm arriving at the same shared secret key even if all inputs are the same.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eLabel values are provided in two forms: where the label value is alphanumeric ASCII, they are represented below as strings.\nFor example, \"MLKEM768-RSAOAEP2048\" below is equivalent to the hexadecimal value \u003ccode\u003e4D4C4B454D3736382D5253414F41455032303438\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSome of the label values contain problematic characters, such as backslashes, that can cause issues displaying correctly in rendered documents or even in source code when the compiler interprets it as an escape character. Below, these are represented directly in hexadecimal. For example, the label for id-MLKEM768-X25519-SHA3-256 is \"\\.//^\\\", but to avoid transcription errors it is provided only in hexadecimal as \u003ccode\u003e5c2e2f2f5e5c\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite KEM algorithm list:\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{::include src/algParams.md}\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn alignment with ML-KEM [FIPS.203], Composite KEM algorithms output a 256-bit shared secret key at all security levels.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor all RSA key types and sizes, the exponent is RECOMMENDED to be 65537. Implementations MAY support only 65537 and reject other exponent values. Legacy RSA implementations that use other values for the exponent MAY be used within a composite, but need to be careful when interoperating with other implementations.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSHA3-256 is used as the KDF for all Composite ML-KEM algorithms.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eRSA-OAEP Parameters {#sect-rsaoaep-params}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-rsa-oaep-parameters-sect-rsaoaep-params\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: RSA-OAEP Parameters {#sect-rsaoaep-params}\" href=\"#rsa-oaep-parameters-sect-rsaoaep-params\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUse of RSA-OAEP [RFC8017] requires additional parameters to be specified.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe RSA component keys MUST be generated at the specified 2048-bit, 3072-bit, 4096-bit key sizes respectively (up to small differences such as dropping leading zeros); intermediate sizes are not acceptable.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAs with the other Composite ML-KEM algorithms, AlgorithmIdentifier parameters MUST be absent. The RSA-OAEP primitive SHALL be instantiated with the following hard-coded parameters which are the same for the 2048, 3072 and 4096 bit key sizes since the objective is to carry and output a 256-bit shared secret key at all security levels.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cmarkdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eRSAES-OAEP-params\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eValue\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003ehashAlgorithm\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eid-sha256\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eMaskGenAlgorithm.algorithm\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eid-mgf1\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003emaskGenAlgorithm.parameters\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eid-sha256\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003epSourceAlgorithm\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003epSpecifiedEmpty\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003ess_len\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e256 bits\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e{: #rsa-oaep-params title=\"RSA-OAEP Parameters\"}\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/markdown-accessiblity-table\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFull specifications for the referenced algorithms can be found in {{appdx_components}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote: The mask length, according to [RFC8017], is \u003ccode\u003ek - hLen - 1\u003c/code\u003e, where \u003ccode\u003ek\u003c/code\u003e is the size of the RSA modulus. Since the choice of hash function and the RSA key size is fixed for each composite algorithm, implementations could choose to pre-compute and hard-code the mask length.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eRationale for choices {#sec-rationale}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-rationale-for-choices-sec-rationale\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Rationale for choices {#sec-rationale}\" href=\"#rationale-for-choices-sec-rationale\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn generating the list of composite algorithms, the idea was to provide composite algorithms at various security levels with varying performance characteristics.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe main design consideration in choosing pairings is to prioritize providing pairings of each ML-KEM security level with commonly-deployed traditional algorithms. This supports the design goal of using composites as a stepping stone to efficiently deploy post-quantum on top of existing hardened and certified traditional algorithm implementations. This was prioritized rather than attempting to exactly match the security level of the post-quantum and traditional components -- which in general is difficult to do since there is no academic consensus on how to compare the \"bits of security\" against classical attackers and \"qubits of security\" against quantum attackers.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhile it may seem odd to use 256-bit outputs at all security levels, this aligns with ML-KEM [FIPS.203] which produces a 256-bit shared secret key at all security levels. SHA3-256 has 256 bits of (2nd) pre-image resistance, which is the required property for a KDF to provide 128 bits of security, as allowed in Table 3 of {{SP.800-57pt1r5}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eASN.1 Module {#sec-asn1-module}\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca dir=\"auto\"\u003eSecurity Considerations {#sec-cons}\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-security-considerations-sec-cons\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Security Considerations {#sec-cons}\" href=\"#security-considerations-sec-cons\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAs this specification uses ML-KEM as a component of all composite algorithms, all security considerations from {{I-D.ietf-lamps-kyber-certificates}} and {{I-D.sfluhrer-cfrg-ml-kem-security-considerations}} apply. Note in particular the \"Encapsulation key check\" in section 7.2 of [FIPS.203] and the \"Decapsulation input check\" in section 7.3 of [FIPS.203] which are required for correct and secure functioning of ML-KEM, but which are considered to be external to the \u003ccode\u003eEncaps()\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eDecaps()\u003c/code\u003e algorithms.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy Hybrids?\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-hybrids\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why Hybrids?\" href=\"#why-hybrids\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn broad terms, a PQ/T Hybrid can be used either to provide dual-algorithm security or to provide migration flexibility. Let's quickly explore both.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDual-algorithm security. The general idea is that the data is protected by two algorithms such that an attacker would need to break both in order to compromise the data. As with most of cryptography, this property is easy to state in general terms, but becomes more complicated when expressed in formalisms. The following sections go into more detail here.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMigration flexibility. Some PQ/T hybrids exist to provide a sort of \"OR\" mode where the application can choose to use one algorithm or the other or both. The intention is that the PQ/T hybrid mechanism builds in application backwards compatibility to allow legacy and upgraded applications to co-exist and communicate. The composite algorithms presented in this specification do not provide this since they operate in a strict \"AND\" mode. They do, however, provide codebase migration flexibility. Consider that an organization has today a mature, validated, certified, hardened implementation of RSA or ECC; composites allow them to add an ML-KEM implementation which immediately starts providing benefits against harvest-now-decrypt-later attacks even if that ML-KEM implementation is still an experimental, non-validated, non-certified, non-hardened implementation. More details of obtaining FIPS certification of a composite algorithm can be found in {{sec-fips}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eKEM Combiner {#sec-cons-kem-combiner}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-kem-combiner-sec-cons-kem-combiner\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: KEM Combiner {#sec-cons-kem-combiner}\" href=\"#kem-combiner-sec-cons-kem-combiner\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe KEM combiner from {{sec-kem-combiner}} is reproduced here for reference.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"  SHA3-256(mlkemSS || tradSS || tradCT || tradPK || Label)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e  SHA3-256(mlkemSS || tradSS || tradCT || tradPK || Label)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{: #code-generic-kem-combiner title=\"KEM combiner construction\"}\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe primary security property of the KEM combiner is that it preserves indistinguishable (adaptive) chosen-ciphertext (IND-CCA2) security of the overall Composite ML-KEM so long as at least one component is IND-CCA2 {{X-Wing}} [GHP18]. Additionally, we also need to consider the case where one of the component algorithms is completely broken; that the private key is known to an attacker. In this case, we rely on the construction of the KEM combiner to ensure that the value of the other shared secret key cannot be leaked or the combined shared secret key predicted via manipulation of the broken algorithm.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eEach registered Composite ML-KEM algorithm specifies a \u003ccode\u003eLabel\u003c/code\u003e -- see {{sec-alg-parms}}. Given that each Composite ML-KEM algorithm fully specifies the component algorithms, including for example the size of the RSA modulus, all inputs to the KEM combiner are fixed-size and thus do not require length-prefixing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003emlkemSS\u003c/code\u003e is always 32 bytes.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etradSS\u003c/code\u003e in the case of DH this is derived by the decapsulator and therefore the length is not controlled by the attacker, however in the case of RSA-OAEP this value is directly chosen by the sender and both the length and content could be freely chosen by an attacker.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etradCT\u003c/code\u003e is either an elliptic curve public key or an RSA-OAEP ciphertext which is required to have its length checked by step 1b of RSAES-OAEP-DECRYPT in [RFC8017].\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etradPK\u003c/code\u003e is the public key of the traditional component (elliptic curve or RSA) and therefore fixed-length.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eLabel\u003c/code\u003e is a fixed value specified in this document.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eIND-CCA2 Security of the hybrid scheme {#sec-hybrid-security}\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-ind-cca2-security-of-the-hybrid-scheme-sec-hybrid-security\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: IND-CCA2 Security of the hybrid scheme {#sec-hybrid-security}\" href=\"#ind-cca2-security-of-the-hybrid-scheme-sec-hybrid-security\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eInformally, a Composite ML-KEM algorithm is secure if the combiner (SHA3) is secure, and either ML-KEM is secure or the traditional component (RSA-OAEP, ECDH, X25519 or X448) is secure.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe security of ML-KEM and DH hybrids is covered in [X-Wing] and requires that the first KEM component (ML-KEM in this construction) is IND-CCA2 and second ciphertext preimage resistant (C2PRI) and that the DH component is nominal group; i.e. a well-behaved elliptic curve DH group, but does not require the traditional component to be IND-CCA. This design choice improves performance by not including the large ML-KEM public key and ciphertext, but means that an implementation error in the ML-KEM component that affects the ciphertext check step of the FO transform could result in the overall composite no longer achieving IND-CCA2 security. This solution remains IND-CCA2 due to binding the \u003ccode\u003etradPK\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003etradCT\u003c/code\u003e in the KEM combiner.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe QSF framework presented in [X-Wing] is extended to cover RSA-OAEP as the traditional algorithm in place of DH by noting that RSA-OAEP is also IND-CCA2 secure [RFC8017].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe composite combiner cannot be assumed to be secure when used with different KEMs and a more cautious approach would bind the public key and ciphertext of the first KEM as well.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eSecond pre-image resistance of component KEMs {#sec-cons-ct-collision}\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-second-pre-image-resistance-of-component-kems-sec-cons-ct-collision\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Second pre-image resistance of component KEMs {#sec-cons-ct-collision}\" href=\"#second-pre-image-resistance-of-component-kems-sec-cons-ct-collision\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe notion of a \"ciphertext second pre-image resistant KEM\" is defined in [X-Wing] as being the property that it is computationally difficult to find two different ciphertexts \u003ccode\u003ec != c'\u003c/code\u003e that will decapsulate to the same shared secret key under the same public key. For the purposes of a hybrid KEM combiner, this property means that given two composite ciphertexts \u003ccode\u003e(c1, c2)\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e(c1', c2')\u003c/code\u003e, we must obtain a unique overall shared secret key so long as either \u003ccode\u003ec1 != c1'\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ec2 != c2'\u003c/code\u003e -- i.e. the overall Composite ML-KEM is ciphertext second pre-image resistant, and therefore secure so long as one of the component KEMs is secure.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn [X-Wing] it is proven that ML-KEM is a second pre-image resistant KEM and therefore the ML-KEM ciphertext can safely be omitted from the KEM combiner. Note that this makes a fundamental assumption on ML-KEM remaining ciphertext second pre-image resistant, and therefore this formulation of KEM combiner does not fully protect against implementation errors in the ML-KEM component -- particularly around the ciphertext check step of the Fujisaki-Okamoto transform -- which could trivially lead to second ciphertext pre-image attacks that break the IND-CCA2 security of the ML-KEM component and of the overall Composite ML-KEM. This could be more fully mitigated by binding the ML-KEM ciphertext in the combiner, but a design decision was made to settle for protection against algorithmic attacks and not implementation attacks against ML-KEM in order to increase performance.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHowever, since neither RSA-OAEP nor DH guarantee second pre-image resistance at all, even in a correct implementation, these ciphertexts are bound to the key derivation in order to guarantee that \u003ccode\u003ec != c'\u003c/code\u003e will yield a unique ciphertext, and thus restoring second pre-image resistance to the overall Composite ML-KEM.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eGenerifying this construction\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-generifying-this-construction\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Generifying this construction\" href=\"#generifying-this-construction\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIt should be clear that the security analysis of the presented KEM combiner construction relies heavily on the specific choices of component algorithms and combiner KDF, and this combiner construction SHOULD NOT by applied to any other combination of ciphers without performing the appropriate security analysis.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eKey Reuse {#sec-cons-key-reuse}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-key-reuse-sec-cons-key-reuse\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Key Reuse {#sec-cons-key-reuse}\" href=\"#key-reuse-sec-cons-key-reuse\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhile conformance with this specification requires that both components of a composite key MUST be freshly generated, the designers are aware that some implementers may be forced to break this rule due to operational constraints. This section documents the implications of doing so.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen using single-algorithm cryptography, the best practice is to always generate fresh keying material for each purpose, for example when renewing a certificate, or obtaining both a TLS and S/MIME certificate for the same device. However, in practice key reuse in such scenarios is not always catastrophic to security and therefore often tolerated. However this reasoning does not hold in the PQ/T hybrid setting.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWithin the broader context of PQ/T hybrids, we need to consider new attack surfaces that arise due to the hybrid constructions and did not exist in single-algorithm contexts. One of these is key reuse where the component keys within a hybrid are also used by themselves within a single-algorithm context. For example, it might be tempting for an operator to take already-deployed RSA keys and add an ML-KEM key to them to form a hybrid. Within a hybrid signature context this leads to a class of attacks referred to as \"stripping attacks\" where one component signature can be extracted and presented as a single-algorithm signature. Hybrid KEMs using a concatenation-style KEM combiner, as is done in this specification, do not have the analogous attack surface because even if an attacker is able to extract and decrypt one of the component ciphertexts, this will yield a different shared secret key than the overall shared secret key derived from the composite, so any subsequent symmetric cryptographic operations will fail.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn addition, there is a further implication to key reuse regarding certificate revocation. Upon receiving a new certificate enrolment request, many certification authorities will check if the requested public key has been previously revoked due to key compromise. Often a CA will perform this check by using the public key hash. Therefore, if one, or even both, components of a composite have been previously revoked, the CA may only check the hash of the combined composite key and not find the revocations. Therefore, because the possibility of key reuse exists even though forbidden in this specification, CAs performing revocation checks on a composite key SHOULD also check both component keys independently to verify that the component keys have not been revoked.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePolicy for Deprecated and Acceptable Algorithms\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-policy-for-deprecated-and-acceptable-algorithms\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Policy for Deprecated and Acceptable Algorithms\" href=\"#policy-for-deprecated-and-acceptable-algorithms\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTraditionally, a public key or certificate contains a single cryptographic algorithm. If and when an algorithm becomes deprecated (for example, RSA-512, or SHA1), the path to deprecating it through policy and removing it from operational environments is, at least is principle, straightforward.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn the composite model this is less obvious since a PQ/T hybrid is expected to still be considered valid after the traditional component is deprecated for individual use. As such, a single composite public key or certificate may contain a mixture of deprecated and non-deprecated algorithms. In general this should be manageable through policy by removing OIDs for the standalone component algorithms while still allowing OIDs for composite algorithms. However, complications may arise when the composite implementation needs to invoke the cryptographic module for a deprecated component algorithm. In particular, this could lead to complex Cryptographic Bills of Materials that show implementations of deprecated algorithms still present and being used.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eImplementation Considerations {#sec-in-pract}\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-implementation-considerations-sec-in-pract\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Implementation Considerations {#sec-in-pract}\" href=\"#implementation-considerations-sec-in-pract\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eFIPS Certification {#sec-fips}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-fips-certification-sec-fips\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: FIPS Certification {#sec-fips}\" href=\"#fips-certification-sec-fips\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following sections give guidance to implementers wishing to FIPS-certify a composite implementation.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis guidance is not authoritative and has not been endorsed by NIST.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eImplementers seeking FIPS certification of a composite KEM algorithm where only one of the component algorithms has been FIPS-validated or FIPS-approved should credit the FIPS-validated component algorithm with full security strength, the non-FIPS-validated component algorithm with zero security, and the overall composite should be considered at least as strong and thus FIPS-approved.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe composite algorithm has been designed to treat the underlying primitives as \"black-box implementations\" and not impose any additional requirements on them that could require an existing implementation of an underlying primitive to run in a mode different from the one under which it was certified. For example, the \u003ccode\u003eKeyGen\u003c/code\u003e defined in {{sec-keygen}} invokes \u003ccode\u003eML-KEM.KeyGen_internal(d, z)\u003c/code\u003e which might not be available in a cryptographic module running in FIPS-mode, but {{sec-keygen}} is only a suggested implementation and the composite KeyGen MAY be implemented using a different available interface for ML-KEM.KeyGen.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe authors wish to note that composite algorithms provide a design pattern to provide utility in future situations that require care to remain FIPS-compliant, such as future cryptographic migrations as well as bridging across jurisdictions with non-intersecting cryptographic requirements.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSuccessful FIPS certification will need to take into account the \"Encapsulation key check\" in section 7.2 of [FIPS.203] and the \"Decapsulation input check\" in section 7.3 of [FIPS.203] which are required for correct and secure functioning of ML-KEM, but which are considered to be external to the \u003ccode\u003eEncaps()\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eDecaps()\u003c/code\u003e algorithms.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following sections go into further detail on specific issues that relate to FIPS certification.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eCombiner Function\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-combiner-function\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Combiner Function\" href=\"#combiner-function\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor reference, the KEM combiner used in Composite ML-KEM is:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"ss = SHA3-256(mlkemSS || tradSS || tradCT || tradPK || Label)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ess = SHA3-256(mlkemSS || tradSS || tradCT || tradPK || Label)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNIST SP 800-227 [SP800-227] allows hybrid key combiners of the following form:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"K \u0026lt;- KDM((S1,S2,...,St), OtherInput)           (14)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eK \u0026lt;- KDM((S1,S2,...,St), OtherInput)           (14)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eComposite ML-KEM maps cleanly into this since it places the two shared secret keys \u003ccode\u003emlkemSS || tradSS\u003c/code\u003e at the beginning of the KDF input such that all other inputs \u003ccode\u003etradCT || tradPK || Label\u003c/code\u003e can be considered part of \u003ccode\u003eOtherInput\u003c/code\u003e for the purposes of FIPS certification.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor the detailed steps of the Key Derivation Mechanism KDM, [SP800-227] refers to [SP.800-56Cr2].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eCompliance of the Composite ML-KEM variants is achieved in the following way:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe Composite ML-KEM algorithms use SHA3, and so can be certified under [SP.800-56Cr2] One-Step Key Derivation Option 1: \u003ccode\u003eH(x) = hash(x)\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e[SP.800-56Cr2] section 4 \"One-Step Key Derivation\" requires a \u003ccode\u003ecounter\u003c/code\u003e which begins at the 4-byte value 0x00000001. However, the counter is allowed to be omitted when the hash function is executed only once, as specified on page 159 of the FIPS 140-3 Implementation Guidance [FIPS-140-3-IG].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eOrder of KDF inputs with Non-Approved Algorithms\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-order-of-kdf-inputs-with-non-approved-algorithms\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Order of KDF inputs with Non-Approved Algorithms\" href=\"#order-of-kdf-inputs-with-non-approved-algorithms\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e[SP800-227] adds an important stipulation that was not present in earlier NIST specifications:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis publication approves the use of the key combiner (14) for any t \u0026gt; 1, so long as at\nleast one shared secret (i.e., S_j for some j) is a shared secret generated from the key-\nestablishment methods of SP 800-56A or SP 800-56B, or an approved KEM.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis means that although Composite ML-KEM always places the shared secret key from ML-KEM in the first slot, a Composite ML-KEM can be FIPS certified so long as either component is FIPS certified. This is important for several reasons. First, in the early stages of PQC migration, composites allow for a non-FIPS certified ML-KEM implementation to be added to a module that already has a FIPS certified traditional component, and the resulting composite can be FIPS certified. Second, when eventually RSA and Elliptic Curve are no longer FIPS-allowed, the composite can retain its FIPS certified status on the strength of the ML-KEM component. Third, while this is outside the scope of this specification, the general composite construction could be used to create FIPS certified algorithms that contain a component algorithm from a different jurisdiction. Third, a composite where both components are FIPS-certified could allow an implementer to patch one component algorithm while awaiting re-certification while continuing to use the overall composite in FIPS mode.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote that before [SP800-227] was in force, [SP.800-56Cr2] required the shared secret key from the certified algorithm to be in the first slot and therefore a Composite ML-KEM implementation using a FIPS-certified traditional component and a non-FIPS certified ML-KEM is not believed to be certifiable under [SP.800-56Cr2] alone, and requires the ammendments made by [SP800-227].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eBackwards Compatibility {#sec-backwards-compat}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-backwards-compatibility-sec-backwards-compat\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Backwards Compatibility {#sec-backwards-compat}\" href=\"#backwards-compatibility-sec-backwards-compat\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe term \"application backwards compatibility\" is used here to mean that existing systems as they are deployed today can interoperate with the upgraded systems of the future.  This draft explicitly does not provide application backwards compatibility, only upgraded systems will understand the OIDs defined in this specification.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThese migration and interoperability concerns need to be thought about in the context of various types of protocols that make use of X.509 and PKIX with relation to key establishment and content encryption, from online negotiated protocols such as TLS 1.3 [RFC8446] and IKEv2 [RFC7296], to non-negotiated asynchronous protocols such as S/MIME signed email [RFC8551], as well as myriad other standardized and proprietary protocols and applications that leverage CMS [RFC5652] encrypted structures.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eProfiling down the number of options {#sec-impl-profile}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-profiling-down-the-number-of-options-sec-impl-profile\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Profiling down the number of options {#sec-impl-profile}\" href=\"#profiling-down-the-number-of-options-sec-impl-profile\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOne daunting aspect of this specification is the number of composite algorithm combinations.\nEach option has been specified because there is a community that has a direct application for it; typically because the traditional component is already deployed in a change-managed environment, or because that specific traditional component is required for regulatory reasons.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eHowever, this large number of combinations leads either to fracturing of the ecosystem into non-interoperable sub-groups when different communities choose non-overlapping subsets to support, or on the other hand it leads to spreading development resources too thin when trying to support all options.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis specification does not list any particular composite algorithm as mandatory-to-implement, however organizations that operate within specific application domains are encouraged to define profiles that select a small number of composites appropriate for that application domain.\nFor applications that do not have any regulatory requirements or legacy implementations to consider, it is RECOMMENDED to focus implementation effort on:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"id-MLKEM768-X25519-SHA3-256  (aka \u0026quot;X-Wing\u0026quot;)\nid-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eid-MLKEM768-X25519-SHA3-256  (aka \"X-Wing\")\nid-MLKEM768-ECDH-P256-SHA3-256\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn applications that only allow NIST PQC Level 5, it is RECOMMENDED to focus implementation effort on:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"id-MLKEM1024-ECDH-P384-SHA3-256\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eid-MLKEM1024-ECDH-P384-SHA3-256\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eDecapsulation Requires the Public Key {#impl-cons-decaps-pubkey}\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-decapsulation-requires-the-public-key-impl-cons-decaps-pubkey\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Decapsulation Requires the Public Key {#impl-cons-decaps-pubkey}\" href=\"#decapsulation-requires-the-public-key-impl-cons-decaps-pubkey\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eML-KEM always requires the public key in order to perform various steps of the Fujisaki-Okamoto decapsulation [FIPS.203], and for this reason the private key encoding specified in FIPS 203 includes the public key.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMoreover, the KEM combiner as specified in {{sec-kem-combiner}} requires the public key of the traditional component in order to achieve the public-key binding property and ciphertext collision resistance as described in {{sec-cons-kem-combiner}}. Since \u003ccode\u003etradPK\u003c/code\u003e is not carried in the composite private key encoding, the implementation is required to obtain it from some out-of-band mechanism. This section discusses several options, but is a non-normative, non-exhaustive list.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDerive or extract from private key. Many cryptographic modules expose functionality to obtain an RSA or EC public key from the corresponding private key. For applications where such functionality does not exist, {{sec-rsa-pub-from-priv}} and {{sec-ec-pub-from-priv}} provide the suggested mechanisms for extracting the public keys from private keys for RSA and ECDH respectively. It is assumed that this is not required for X25519 or X448 since those private keys are seeds from which the public key can be obtained.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFetch it from an external data source, for example from the public-key certificate corresponding to this private key.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIf the composite KEM private key is being carried within a PKCS#8 OneAsymmetricKey object, place the full composite public key within the optional OneAsymmetricKey.publicKey field, which allows extracting the tradPK (and re-encode as necessary for correctly using it in the KEM Combiner).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUse an alternate private key encoding that explicitly carries the tradPK.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eExtracting RSAPublicKey from RSAPrivateKey {#sec-rsa-pub-from-priv}\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-extracting-rsapublickey-from-rsaprivatekey-sec-rsa-pub-from-priv\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Extracting RSAPublicKey from RSAPrivateKey {#sec-rsa-pub-from-priv}\" href=\"#extracting-rsapublickey-from-rsaprivatekey-sec-rsa-pub-from-priv\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAssuming that the RSA component of the composite private key is encoded as an RSAPrivateKey, as required by this specification, then, quoting from [RFC8017] you have:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"RSAPrivateKey ::= SEQUENCE {\n    version           Version,\n    modulus           INTEGER,  -- n\n    publicExponent    INTEGER,  -- e\n    privateExponent   INTEGER,  -- d\n    prime1            INTEGER,  -- p\n    prime2            INTEGER,  -- q\n    exponent1         INTEGER,  -- d mod (p-1)\n    exponent2         INTEGER,  -- d mod (q-1)\n    coefficient       INTEGER,  -- (inverse of q) mod p\n    otherPrimeInfos   OtherPrimeInfos OPTIONAL\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eRSAPrivateKey ::= SEQUENCE {\n    version           Version,\n    modulus           INTEGER,  -- n\n    publicExponent    INTEGER,  -- e\n    privateExponent   INTEGER,  -- d\n    prime1            INTEGER,  -- p\n    prime2            INTEGER,  -- q\n    exponent1         INTEGER,  -- d mod (p-1)\n    exponent2         INTEGER,  -- d mod (q-1)\n    coefficient       INTEGER,  -- (inverse of q) mod p\n    otherPrimeInfos   OtherPrimeInfos OPTIONAL\n}\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis can trivially be converted into an RSAPublicKey through simple DER decoding / re-encoding since both required values are already present.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"RSAPublicKey ::= SEQUENCE {\n    modulus           INTEGER,  -- n\n    publicExponent    INTEGER   -- e\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eRSAPublicKey ::= SEQUENCE {\n    modulus           INTEGER,  -- n\n    publicExponent    INTEGER   -- e\n}\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eDeriving the public ECPoint from ECPrivateKey {#sec-ec-pub-from-priv}\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-deriving-the-public-ecpoint-from-ecprivatekey-sec-ec-pub-from-priv\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Deriving the public ECPoint from ECPrivateKey {#sec-ec-pub-from-priv}\" href=\"#deriving-the-public-ecpoint-from-ecprivatekey-sec-ec-pub-from-priv\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUnlike RSA, the ECPrivateKey does not contain sufficient information to simply extract the public key. Note that in the interest of having a single unique encoding to foster interoperability, this specification forbids the optional \u003ccode\u003epublicKey\u003c/code\u003e field.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThat said, the EC public key can be derived from the private key in the following way:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"g = generator for the group P256r1, P384r1, etc.\ns = ECPrivateKey.getS()\n\npubKey = ec_multiply_by_scalar(g, s)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eg = generator for the group P256r1, P384r1, etc.\ns = ECPrivateKey.getS()\n\npubKey = ec_multiply_by_scalar(g, s)\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003ewhere a recommended implementation of \u003ccode\u003eec_multiply_by_scalar()\u003c/code\u003e can be found in [SEC1].\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThen encode \u003ccode\u003epubKey\u003c/code\u003e as X9.62 uncompressed point.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e--- 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe sizes listed below are maximum values: several factors could cause fluctuations in the size of the traditional component. For example, this could be due to:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe RSA public key \u003ccode\u003e(n, e)\u003c/code\u003e allows \u003ccode\u003ee\u003c/code\u003e to vary in size between 3 and \u003ccode\u003en - 1\u003c/code\u003e [RFC8017]. Note that the size table below assumes the recommended value of \u003ccode\u003ee = 65537\u003c/code\u003e, so for RSA combinations it is in fact not a true maximum.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWhen the underlying RSA or EC value is itself DER-encoded, integer values could occasionally be shorter than expected due to leading zeros being dropped from the encoding.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBy contrast, ML-KEM values are always fixed size, so composite values can always be correctly de-serialized based on the size of the ML-KEM component.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSize values marked with an asterisk (*) in the table are not fixed but maximum possible values for the composite key or ciphertext. Implementations MUST NOT perform strict length checking based on such values.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNon-hybrid ML-KEM is included for reference.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e{::include src/sizeTable.md}\n{: #tab-size-values title=\"Maximum size values of composite ML-KEM\"}\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMany cryptographic libraries are X.509-focused and do not expose interfaces to instantiate a public key from raw bytes, but only from a SubjectPublicKeyInfo structure as you would find in an X.509 certificate, therefore implementing Composite ML-KEM in those libraries requires reconstructing the SPKI for each component algorithm. In order to aid implementers and reduce interoperability issues, this section lists out the full public key for each component algorithm.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eML-KEM-768\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" 02\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eASN.1:\n  algorithm AlgorithmIdentifier ::= {\n    algorithm id-alg-ml-kem-768   -- (2.16.840.1.101.3.4.4.2)\n    }\n\nDER:\n  30 0B 06
