0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis specification borrows extensively from the analysis and KEM combiner construction presented in [X-Wing]. In particular, X-Wing and id-MLKEM768-X25519-SHA3-256 are largely interchangeable. The one difference is that X-Wing uses a combined KeyGen function to generate the two component private keys from the same seed, which gives some additional binding properties. In order to allow for re-use of existing hardeneded certified cryptographic modules (for example, getting the RSA component from an existing smartcard), this specification keeps the key generation for both components separate and only loosely-specified so that implementers are free to use an existing certified hardware or software module for one or both components.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eETSI CatKDF\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-etsi-catkdf\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: ETSI CatKDF\" href=\"#etsi-catkdf\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e[ETSI.TS.103.744] section 8.2.3 defines CatKDF as:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"1) Form secret = psk || k1 || k2.\n2) Set context = f(info, MA, MB), where f is a context formatting\n   function.\n3) key_material = KDF(secret, label, context, length).\n4) Return key_material.\n\nMA shall contain all of the public keys.\nMB shall contain all of the corresponding public keys and ciphertexts.\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e1) Form secret = psk || k1 || k2.\n2) Set context = f(info, MA, MB), where f is a context formatting\n   function.\n3) key_material = KDF(secret, label, context, length).\n4) Return key_material.\n\nMA shall contain all of the public keys.\nMB shall contain all of the corresponding public keys and ciphertexts.\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe main difference between the Composite ML-KEM combiner and the ETSI CatKDF combiner is that CatKDF makes the more conservative choice to bind the public keys and ciphertexts of both components, while Composite ML-KEM follows the analysis presented in [X-Wing] that while preserving the security properties of the traditional component requires binding the public key and ciphertext of the traditional component, it is not necessary to do so for ML-KEM thanks to the rejection sampling step of the Fujisaki-Okamoto transform.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAdditionally, ETSI CatKDF can be instantiated with either HMAC [RFC2104], KMAC [SP.800-185] or HKDF [RFC5869] as KDF. Since this specification uses SHA3-256 as the KDF for all variants, there is no equivalent construction of CatKDF.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eExamples of KEM Combiner Intermediate Values\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-examples-of-kem-combiner-intermediate-values\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Examples of KEM Combiner Intermediate Values\" href=\"#examples-of-kem-combiner-intermediate-values\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis section provides examples of constructing the input for the KEM Combiner, showing all intermediate values. This is intended to be useful for debugging purposes. See {{sec-kem-combiner}} for additional information.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eEach input component is shown. Note that values are shown hex-encoded for display purposes only, they are actually raw binary values.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003emlkemSS\u003c/code\u003e is the shared secret produced by the ML-KEM encapsulate or decapsulate function which is always 32 bytes.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etradSS\u003c/code\u003e is the shared secret produce by the traditional algorithm.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etradCT\u003c/code\u003e is either an elliptic curve public key or an RSA-OAEP ciphertext depending on the algorithm chosen.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etradPK\u003c/code\u003e is the public key of the traditional component (elliptic curve or RSA) and therefore fixed-length.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eLabel\u003c/code\u003e is the specific KEM Combiner Label for this composite algorithm.  See {{sec-alg-parms}}\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eNext, the \u003ccode\u003eCombined KDF Input\u003c/code\u003e is given, which is simply the concatenation of the above values.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFinally, the \u003ccode\u003eKDF Function\u003c/code\u003e and the \u003ccode\u003ess Output\u003c/code\u003e are shown as outputs.  The \u003ccode\u003ess\u003c/code\u003e is the Composite ML-KEM shared-secret generated by applying the KDF to the \u003ccode\u003eCombined KDF Input\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eExamples are given for each recommended Composite ML-KEM algorithm from {{sec-impl-profile}}.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eExample 1:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"{::include ./src/kemCombiner_MLKEM768_ECDH_P256_SHA3_256.md}\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e{::include ./src/kemCombiner_MLKEM768_ECDH_P256_SHA3_256.md}\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eExample 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe following test vectors are provided in a format similar to the NIST ACVP Known-Answer-Tests (KATs).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe structure is that a global \u003ccode\u003ecacert\u003c/code\u003e is provided which is used to sign each KEM certificate.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWithin each test case there are the following values:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etcId\u003c/code\u003e the name of the algorithm.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eek\u003c/code\u003e the encapsulation public key.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ex5c\u003c/code\u003e the X.509 certificate of the encapsulation key, signed by the cacert.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003edk\u003c/code\u003e the raw decapsulation private key.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003edk_pkcs8\u003c/code\u003e the decapsulation private key in a PKCS#8 object.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ec\u003c/code\u003e the ciphertext.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ek\u003c/code\u003e the derived shared secret key.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eImplementers should be able to perform the following tests using the test vectors below:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eLoad the public key \u003ccode\u003eek\u003c/code\u003e or certificate \u003ccode\u003ex5c\u003c/code\u003e and perform an encapsulation for it (you should obtain valid \u003ccode\u003ect\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ek\u003c/code\u003e values, but they will not match the ones in the test vector since \u003ccode\u003eEncap()\u003c/code\u003e is randomized.)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eLoad the decapsulation private key \u003ccode\u003edk\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003edk_pkcs8\u003c/code\u003e and the ciphertext \u003ccode\u003ec\u003c/code\u003e and perform a \u003ccode\u003eDecaps()\u003c/code\u003e operation to ensure that the same shared secret key \u003ccode\u003ek\u003c/code\u003e is derived.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTest vectors are provided for each underlying ML-KEM algorithm in isolation for the purposes of debugging.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDue to the length of the test vectors, some readers will prefer to retrieve the non-word-wrapped copy from GitHub {{TestVectors}}. The reference implementation written in python that generated them is also available.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"{::include src/testvectors_wrapped.json}\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e{::include src/testvectors_wrapped.json}\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eContributors and Acknowledgments\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-contributors-and-acknowledgments\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Contributors and Acknowledgments\" href=\"#contributors-and-acknowledgments\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis document represents the results of a many-year effort by the LAMPS working group.
